An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state. One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object. That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-100\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package cache\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"errors\"\n21: \t\"fmt\"\n22: \t\"sync\"\n23: \t\"time\"\n24: \n25: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n26: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n27: \tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n28: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n29: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n30: \t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n31: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n32: \n33: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n34: \n35: \tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n36: )\n37: \n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n47: //\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n52: //\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n65: // selector.\n66: //\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n73: //\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n75: // during `Run()`.\n76: //\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\n84: //\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n91: //\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n96: // into its constituent parts.\n97: //\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0@8e5772e5b95a59b265a3b48c5fe5a7d1e163cf69/-/blob/tools/cache/shared_informer.go%3FL1-100"}}}

For every\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n127: //\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n131: // to something else, for example through a\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n133: //\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\n138: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n139: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n140: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n141: \t// different handlers.\n142: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n143: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n144: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n145: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n146: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n147: \t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n148: \t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n149: \t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n150: \t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n151: \t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\n152: \t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\n153: \t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\n154: \t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\n155: \t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\n156: \t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\n157: \t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\n158: \t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\n159: \t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\n160: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\n161: \t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\n162: \tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n163: \t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\n164: \t// its registration handle.\n165: \t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\n166: \tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\n167: \t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\n168: \tGetStore() Store\n169: \t// GetController is deprecated, it does nothing useful\n170: \tGetController() Controller\n171: \t// Run starts and runs the shared informer, returning after it stops.\n172: \t// The informer will be stopped when stopCh is closed.\n173: \tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n174: \t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\n175: \t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\n176: \t// of the informer's object collection.  This is unrelated to \"resync\".\n177: \t//\n178: \t// Note that this doesn't tell you if an individual handler is synced!!\n179: \t// For that, please call HasSynced on the handle returned by\n180: \t// AddEventHandler.\n181: \tHasSynced() bool\n182: \t// LastSyncResourceVersion is the resource version observed when last synced with the underlying\n183: \t// store. The value returned is not synchronized with access to the underlying store and is not\n184: \t// thread-safe.\n185: \tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n186: \n187: \t// The WatchErrorHandler is called whenever ListAndWatch drops the\n188: \t// connection with an error. After calling this handler, the informer\n189: \t// will backoff and retry.\n190: \t//\n191: \t// The default implementation looks at the error type and tries to log\n192: \t// the error message at an appropriate level.\n193: \t//\n194: \t// There's only one handler, so if you call this multiple times, last one\n195: \t// wins; calling after the informer has been started returns an error.\n196: \t//\n197: \t// The handler is intended for visibility, not to e.g. pause the consumers.\n198: \t// The handler should return quickly - any expensive processing should be\n199: \t// offloaded.\n200: \tSetWatchErrorHandler(handler WatchErrorHandler) error\n201: \n202: \t// The TransformFunc is called for each object which is about to be stored.\n203: \t//\n204: \t// This function is intended for you to take the opportunity to\n205: \t// remove, transform, or normalize fields. \"The SharedInformer factory in Kubernetes client-go implements a sophisticated caching and event distribution system for API server resources. The implementation spans multiple packages and follows a clear architectural pattern.\\n\\n**Factory Layer (informers/factory.go)**: The SharedInformerFactory interface and sharedInformerFactory struct form the top-level API. NewSharedInformerFactory() constructs factories for all Kubernetes API group versions. The factory's Start() method begins all registered informers, running them in goroutines until a stop channel is closed. WaitForCacheSync() polls all started informers' HasSynced() methods until they all return true or the stop channel closes, implementing a polling mechanism with syncedPollPeriod of 100ms.\\n\\n**Informer Implementation (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer struct implements SharedIndexInformer and serves as the core informer. Its Run() method creates a DeltaFIFO queue backed by an Indexer (known objects), constructs a Config for the Controller, and starts two critical components: (1) the Controller which runs the Reflector to pump objects from the API server, and (2) the sharedProcessor which distributes notifications to event handlers. The Run() method also starts a cacheMutationDetector to catch improper mutations of cached objects. The factory maintains sync.RWMutex-protected maps of started informers and tracks which have been started to allow multiple safe Start() calls.\\n\\n**List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go, tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The ListerWatcher interface defines List() and Watch() methods called by the Reflector. ListWatch struct wraps ListFunc and WatchFunc closures that call the API server. The Reflector in tools/cache/reflector.go watches a specified resource and syncs all changes to the DeltaFIFO store. NewReflector() and NewReflectorWithOptions() create Reflectors with configurable backoff, resync periods, and watch timeouts. The Reflector maintains lastSyncResourceVersion thread-safely via RWMutex for pagination and consistency.\\n\\n**Controller and Delta Processing (tools/cache/controller.go, tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The controller struct implements the Controller interface and manages both the Reflector and the processing loop. Its Config struct specifies the Queue (always DeltaFIFO), ListerWatcher, Process function (HandleDeltas), and resync parameters. Run() spawns the Reflector and continuously pops Deltas from the queue, processing them with Config.Process. DeltaFIFO accumulates deltas (Add, Update, Delete, Sync, Replaced) for each object key, keyed by the informer's KeyFunc (usually MetaNamespaceKeyFunc producing 'namespace/name' strings). NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions() accepts KnownObjects (the cache's Indexer) to detect deletions via Replace() calls.\\n\\n**Cache Store (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go, tools/cache/index.go)**: NewIndexer() creates a cache backed by ThreadSafeStore with Indexers for fast lookups. The store is protected by sync.RWMutex and provides eventually consistent access. Indexers map index names to IndexFunc functions that extract index keys from objects. MetaNamespaceIndexFunc is the default indexer extracting namespace from object metadata.\\n\\n**Notification Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor manages processorListener instances for each registered event handler. HandleDeltas() is called by the controller for each delta, updating the cache and calling the processor to distribute notifications. processorListener spawns two goroutines: one buffering notifications from the processor into an unbuffered channel, another draining that channel and dispatching to the actual ResourceEventHandler (AddFunc, UpdateFunc, DeleteFunc). This decouples the slow path (user handlers) from the fast path (informer updates).\\n\\n**Resource-Specific Informers (informers/*/v*/pod.go, etc.)**: Generated code creates resource-specific informer interfaces (PodInformer, NodeInformer) and implementers. Each resource's NewFilteredXyzInformer() creates a ListWatch with closures calling the typed client's List() and Watch() methods, then wraps it in NewSharedIndexInformer(). The factory's InformerFor() deduplicates by caching created informers by reflect.Type.\\n\\n**Generic and Dynamic Informers (informers/generic.go, dynamic/dynamicinformer/informer.go, metadata/metadatainformer/informer.go)**: GenericInformer provides untyped access via schema.GroupVersionResource keys. \"The SharedInformer factory in Kubernetes client-go implements a sophisticated caching and event distribution system for API server resources. The implementation spans multiple packages and follows a clear architectural pattern.\\n\\n**Factory Layer (informers/factory.go)**: The SharedInformerFactory interface and sharedInformerFactory struct form the top-level API. NewSharedInformerFactory() constructs factories for all Kubernetes API group versions. The factory's Start() method begins all registered informers, running them in goroutines until a stop channel is closed. WaitForCacheSync() polls all started informers' HasSynced() methods until they all return true or the stop channel closes, implementing a polling mechanism with syncedPollPeriod of 100ms.\\n\\n**Informer Implementation (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedIndexInformer struct implements SharedIndexInformer and serves as the core informer. Its Run() method creates a DeltaFIFO queue backed by an Indexer (known objects), constructs a Config for the Controller, and starts two critical components: (1) the Controller which runs the Reflector to pump objects from the API server, and (2) the sharedProcessor which distributes notifications to event handlers. The Run() method also starts a cacheMutationDetector to catch improper mutations of cached objects. The factory maintains sync.RWMutex-protected maps of started informers and tracks which have been started to allow multiple safe Start() calls.\\n\\n**List-Watch Mechanism (tools/cache/listwatch.go, tools/cache/reflector.go)**: The ListerWatcher interface defines List() and Watch() methods called by the Reflector. ListWatch struct wraps ListFunc and WatchFunc closures that call the API server. The Reflector in tools/cache/reflector.go watches a specified resource and syncs all changes to the DeltaFIFO store. NewReflector() and NewReflectorWithOptions() create Reflectors with configurable backoff, resync periods, and watch timeouts. The Reflector maintains lastSyncResourceVersion thread-safely via RWMutex for pagination and consistency.\\n\\n**Controller and Delta Processing (tools/cache/controller.go, tools/cache/delta_fifo.go)**: The controller struct implements the Controller interface and manages both the Reflector and the processing loop. Its Config struct specifies the Queue (always DeltaFIFO), ListerWatcher, Process function (HandleDeltas), and resync parameters. Run() spawns the Reflector and continuously pops Deltas from the queue, processing them with Config.Process. DeltaFIFO accumulates deltas (Add, Update, Delete, Sync, Replaced) for each object key, keyed by the informer's KeyFunc (usually MetaNamespaceKeyFunc producing 'namespace/name' strings). NewDeltaFIFOWithOptions() accepts KnownObjects (the cache's Indexer) to detect deletions via Replace() calls.\\n\\n**Cache Store (tools/cache/store.go, tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go, tools/cache/index.go)**: NewIndexer() creates a cache backed by ThreadSafeStore with Indexers for fast lookups. The store is protected by sync.RWMutex and provides eventually consistent access. Indexers map index names to IndexFunc functions that extract index keys from objects. MetaNamespaceIndexFunc is the default indexer extracting namespace from object metadata.\\n\\n**Notification Distribution (tools/cache/shared_informer.go)**: The sharedProcessor manages processorListener instances for each registered event handler. HandleDeltas() is called by the controller for each delta, updating the cache and calling the processor to distribute notifications. processorListener spawns two goroutines: one buffering notifications from the processor into an unbuffered channel, another draining that channel and dispatching to the actual ResourceEventHandler (AddFunc, UpdateFunc, DeleteFunc). This decouples the slow path (user handlers) from the fast path (informer updates).\\n\\n**Resource-Specific Informers (informers/*/v*/pod.go, etc.)**: Generated code creates resource-specific informer interfaces (PodInformer, NodeInformer) and implementers. Each resource's NewFilteredXyzInformer() creates a ListWatch with closures calling the typed client's List() and Watch() methods, then wraps it in NewSharedIndexInformer(). The factory's InformerFor() deduplicates by caching created informers by reflect.Type.\\n\\n**Generic and Dynamic Informers (informers/generic.go, dynamic/dynamicinformer/informer.go, metadata/metadatainformer/informer.go)**: GenericInformer provides untyped access via schema.GroupVersionResource keys. DynamicSharedInformerFactory and metadataSharedInformerFactory follow the same factory pattern but use dynamic.Interface and metadata.Interface clients respectively, enabling dynamic resource watching and lightweight metadata-only caching.\\n\\n**In kubernetes/kubernetes (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/)**: The same implementation exists in the kubernetes repository's staging/src directory, representing the source of truth. All files from tools/cache, informers, dynamic/dynamicinformer, and metadata/metadatainformer packages are present with identical structure.\\n\\nThe key innovation is the separation of concerns: the factory manages lifecycle, the SharedIndexInformer orchestrates components, the Reflector handles API connectivity, the DeltaFIFO tracks changes, and the processor distributes notifications—all working together to maintain an eventually consistent local cache synchronized with the API server state.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
